						<header class="c-article__header">
							<figure class="c-article__figure u-hidden@md">
								<img width="800" height="450" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/20123034/SL-Twelve-featured-800x450.jpg" class="attachment-securelist-2020-thumbnail size-securelist-2020-thumbnail wp-post-image" alt="" decoding="async" fetchpriority="high" data-src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/20123034/SL-Twelve-featured-800x450.jpg" data-srcset="" srcset="" />							</figure>
														<p class="c-article__headline u-hidden@md">
								<a href="https://securelist.com/category/crimeware-reports/" class="c-tag c-tag--primary">Crimeware reports</a>
							</p>
														<h1 class="c-article__title">-=TWELVE=- is back</h1>							<div class="c-article__info">
																<p class="c-article__headline u-hidden u-block@md">
									<a href="https://securelist.com/category/crimeware-reports/" class="c-tag c-tag--primary">Crimeware reports</a>
								</p>
																<p class="u-uppercase"><time datetime="2024-09-20T12:31:34+00:00">20 Sep 2024</time></p>
								<p class="c-article__reading u-ml-auto@md">
									<svg class="o-icon o-svg-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="https://securelist.com/wp-content/themes/securelist2020/assets/sprite/icons.svg#icon-hourglass"></use></svg> <span class="js-reading-time"></span> minute read								</p>
							</div>
						</header>

						<div class="c-article__wrapper">

							<div class="c-article__main">

																<div class="c-highlight c-highlight--overflow-down@md js-accordion u-hidden@md">
									<div class="c-accordion-toggle js-accordion-toggle">
										<div class="c-highlight__header">
											<div class="c-highlight__icon">
												<div class="u-block--theme-light u-hidden--theme-dark">
													<img src="https://securelist.com/wp-content/themes/securelist2020/assets/images/icon/icon-categories.svg" />
												</div>
												<div class="u-block--theme-dark u-hidden--theme-light">
													<img src="https://securelist.com/wp-content/themes/securelist2020/assets/images/icon/icon-categories--invert.svg" />
												</div>
											</div>
											<div class="c-highlight__title">
												<p>Table of Contents</p>
											</div>
										</div>
									</div>
									<div class="js-accordion-container">
										<div class="c-highlight__body">
											<ul class='c-list-links'><li><a href="#about-twelve">About Twelve</a></li><li><a href="#unified-kill-chain-in">Unified Kill Chain: In</a></li><ul class='c-list-links'><li><a href="#reconnaissance">Reconnaissance</a></li><li><a href="#resource-development">Resource Development</a></li><li><a href="#initial-access-and-delivery">Initial Access and Delivery</a></li><li><a href="#exploitation">Exploitation</a></li><ul class='c-list-links'><li><a href="#web-shells">Web shells</a></li><li><a href="#facefish-backdoor">FaceFish backdoor</a></li></ul><li><a href="#persistence">Persistence</a></li><li><a href="#defense-evasion">Defense Evasion</a></li><li><a href="#command-and-control">Command and Control</a></li></ul><li><a href="#unified-kill-chain-through">Unified Kill Chain: Through</a></li><ul class='c-list-links'><li><a href="#pivoting">Pivoting</a></li><li><a href="#discovery">Discovery</a></li><li><a href="#privilege-escalation">Privilege Escalation</a></li><li><a href="#execution">Execution</a></li><ul class='c-list-links'><li><a href="#scripts-and-commands">Scripts and commands</a></li><li><a href="#sophos_kill_local-ps1">Sophos_kill_local.ps1</a></li><li><a href="#using-the-task-scheduler">Using the Task Scheduler</a></li></ul><li><a href="#credential-access">Credential Access</a></li><li><a href="#lateral-movement">Lateral Movement</a></li></ul><li><a href="#unified-kill-chain-out">Unified Kill Chain: Out</a></li><ul class='c-list-links'><li><a href="#collection">Collection</a></li><li><a href="#exfiltration">Exfiltration</a></li><li><a href="#impact">Impact</a></li><ul class='c-list-links'><li><a href="#ransomware">Ransomware</a></li><li><a href="#wipers">Wipers</a></li></ul><li><a href="#objectives">Objectives</a></li></ul><li><a href="#takeaways">Takeaways</a></li><li><a href="#indicators-of-compromise">Indicators of compromise</a></li></ul>										</div>

								<div class="o-row c-article__container">
									<div class="o-col c-article__content js-article-body">
										<div class="js-reading-wrapper">
											<figure class="c-article__figure u-hidden u-block@md">
												<img width="1200" height="600" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/20123034/SL-Twelve-featured-1200x600.jpg" class="attachment-securelist-2020-thumbnail-large size-securelist-2020-thumbnail-large wp-post-image" alt="" decoding="async" loading="lazy" data-src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/20123034/SL-Twelve-featured-1200x600.jpg" data-srcset="" srcset="" />											</figure>

											<div class="c-article__authors u-hidden u-block@md">
												<p class="c-block__title">Authors</p>
												<ul class="c-list-authors">
																<li>
			<a  href="https://securelist.com/author/kaspersky/" >
													<img src="https://securelist.com/wp-content/themes/securelist2020/assets/images/avatar-default/avatar_default_3.png">
										<span>Kaspersky</span></a>
		</li>
														</ul>
											</div>

											
											<div class="js-reading-content">
												<div class="c-wysiwyg">
													<p>In the spring of 2024, posts with real people&#8217;s personal data began appearing on the -=TWELVE=- Telegram channel. Soon it was blocked for falling foul of the Telegram terms of service. The group stayed off the radar for several months, but as we investigated a late June 2024 attack, we found that it employed techniques identical to those of Twelve and relied on C2 servers linked to the threat actor. We are therefore confident that the group is still active and will probably soon resurface. This article uses the <a href="https://unifiedkillchain.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Unified Kill Chain methodology</a> to analyze the attackers&#8217; actions.</p>
<h2 id="about-twelve">About Twelve</h2>
<p>The group was formed in April 2023 in the context of the Russian-Ukrainian conflict and has attacked Russian government organizations ever since.</p>
<p>The threat actor specializes in encrypting and then deleting victims&#8217; data, which seriously complicates efforts to recover the IT environment. This suggests that their main goal is inflicting as much damage as possible. When attacking, the group aims to reach critical assets, but they do not always succeed. In addition, Twelve exfiltrates sensitive information from its victims&#8217; systems and posts it on its Telegram channel.</p>
<p>Interestingly, Twelve shares infrastructure, utilities and techniques (TTPs) with the <a href="https://www.anti-malware.ru/news/2024-02-02-114534/42735" target="_blank" rel="noopener">DARKSTAR</a> ransomware group, formerly known as Shadow or COMET, which suggests that the two belong to the same syndicate or activity cluster. At the same time, whereas Twelve&#8217;s actions are clearly hacktivist in nature, DARKSTAR sticks to the classic double extortion pattern. This variation of objectives within the syndicate underscores the complexity and diversity of modern cyberthreats.</p>
<h2 id="unified-kill-chain-in">Unified Kill Chain: In</h2>
<p>The In stage in terms of the Unified Kill Chain refers to the initial phases of a cyberattack aimed at gaining access to the target organization&#8217;s LAN. These phases include a range of tactical actions: from external reconnaissance to assuming control of the systems inside the protected network.</p>
<h3 id="reconnaissance">Reconnaissance</h3>
<p>While we do not know the exact reconnaissance techniques the threat actor uses, we suspect that they scan IP address ranges across Russia based on geotags and try to identify VPN servers and applications accessible from the internet that could be used as entry points into a target organization&#8217;s or a contractor&#8217;s infrastructure.</p>
<h3 id="resource-development">Resource Development</h3>
<p>As we analyzed the cyberattacks, we found that the threat actor relied exclusively on well-known and freely available tools. The tools frequently used by the group include Cobalt Strike, mimikatz, chisel, BloodHound, PowerView, adPEAS, CrackMapExec, Advanced IP Scanner and PsExec.</p>
<h3 id="initial-access-and-delivery">Initial Access and Delivery</h3>
<p>In most of the attacks we are aware of, the adversary gained initial access to victims&#8217; infrastructure through valid local or domain accounts, VPN or SSH certificates. After gaining access to the victim&#8217;s infrastructure, the attackers used the Remote Desktop Protocol (RDP) to move laterally.</p>
<p>Most times, the attackers penetrated the target infrastructure via some of the victim&#8217;s contractors. To do this, they gained access to the contractor&#8217;s infrastructure and then used its certificate to connect to its customer&#8217;s VPN. Having obtained access to that, the adversary can connect to the customer&#8217;s systems via the Remote Desktop Protocol (RDP) and then penetrate the customer&#8217;s infrastructure.</p>
<p><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19182814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_05.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-113912" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19182814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_05-1024x971.png" alt="" width="1024" height="971" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19182814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_05-1024x971.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19182814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_05-300x285.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19182814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_05-768x729.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19182814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_05-369x350.png 369w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19182814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_05-740x702.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19182814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_05-295x280.png 295w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19182814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_05-800x759.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19182814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_05.png 1422w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a></p>
<h3 id="exploitation">Exploitation</h3>

They could serve various purposes: some executed arbitrary commands, others moved files, and still others, created and sent email. Below are two examples of single-line web shells for moving files.</p>
<p><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183148/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_17.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-113913" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183148/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_17-1024x70.png" alt="Examples of web shells for moving files" width="1024" height="70" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183148/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_17-1024x70.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183148/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_17-300x21.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183148/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_17-768x53.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183148/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_17-1536x105.png 1536w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183148/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_17-740x51.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183148/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_17-1600x109.png 1600w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183148/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_17-800x55.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183148/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_17.png 1916w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a></p>
<div id="attachment_113914" style="width: 1034px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183238/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_13.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113914" class="size-large wp-image-113914" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183238/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_13-1024x53.png" alt="Examples of web shells for moving files" width="1024" height="53" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183238/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_13-1024x53.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183238/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_13-300x16.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183238/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_13-768x40.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183238/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_13-1536x79.png 1536w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183238/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_13-740x38.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183238/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_13-1600x83.png 1600w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183238/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_13-800x41.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183238/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_13.png 1915w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113914" class="wp-caption-text">Examples of web shells for moving files</p></div>
<p>It is worth noting that most of the web shells used by threat actors are publicly available tools that can be found in publicly available sources. Here are two examples:</p>
<ul>
<li>https://github[.]com/stefanpejcic/wordpress-malware;</li>
<li>https://github[.]com/tennc/webshell/blob/master/php/wso/wso2.php.</li>
</ul>
<p>We use the example of a remailer (script for sending email) to examine how the web shells function.</p>
<div id="attachment_113915" style="width: 776px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183339/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_03.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113915" class="size-full wp-image-113915" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183339/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_03.png" alt="Example of a remailer script used by the threat actor" width="766" height="898" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183339/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_03.png 766w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183339/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_03-256x300.png 256w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183339/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_03-299x350.png 299w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183339/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_03-740x868.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183339/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_03-239x280.png 239w" sizes="(max-width: 766px) 100vw, 766px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113915" class="wp-caption-text">Example of a remailer script used by the threat actor</p></div>
<p>The attackers used this PHP script to send email messages. It starts by checking for requisite data, such as the recipient&#8217;s address, subject and message body inside a POST request. If any of the key data is missing, the script reports an error and quits. After successfully checking and preparing email components, it uses the PHP mail() function to send the email.</p>
<h4 id="facefish-backdoor">FaceFish backdoor</h4>
<p>An incident we investigated involved the FaceFish backdoor, loaded with the help of a web shell installed on a VMware vCenter server by exploiting the <a href="https://www.cve.org/CVERecord?id=CVE-2021-21972" target="_blank" rel="noopener">CVE-2021-21972</a> and <a href="https://www.cve.org/CVERecord?id=CVE-2021-22005" target="_blank" rel="noopener">CVE-2021-22005</a> vulnerabilities in the vSphere virtualization platform. The former vulnerability can be found in the platform&#8217;s client and allows remote code execution, while the latter is an arbitrary file upload vulnerability in the server.</p>
<p>Like most of the web shells used by the group, this one is publicly available.</p>
		<div id="crayon-6719ab9d223a5278949935" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-mac print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>

			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>

It was located at the following path in the infected system:</p>

			<div class="crayon-main" style="">

				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-6719ab9d223a6172405937-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6719ab9d223a6172405937-1">/<span class="crayon-i">usr</span>/<span class="crayon-i">lib</span>/<span class="crayon-i">vmware</span>-<span class="crayon-i">vsphere</span>-<span class="crayon-i">ui</span>/<span class="crayon-i">server</span>/<span class="crayon-m">static</span>/<span class="crayon-i">resources</span>/<span class="crayon-i">libs</span>/<span class="crayon-i">shell</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">jsp</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
Once started, FaceFish saves a libs.so shared library in the system, injects it into the sshd process with the ld.so.preload method and restarts the SSH service.</p>
<div id="attachment_113916" style="width: 939px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183618/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_01.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113916" class="size-full wp-image-113916" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183618/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_01.png" alt="Example of FaceFish output" width="929" height="228" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183618/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_01.png 929w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183618/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_01-300x74.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183618/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_01-768x188.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183618/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_01-740x182.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19183618/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_01-800x196.png 800w" sizes="(max-width: 929px) 100vw, 929px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113916" class="wp-caption-text">Example of FaceFish output</p></div>
<h3 id="persistence">Persistence</h3>
<p>To gain a foothold in the domain infrastructure, the adversary used PowerShell to add domain users and groups, and to modify ACLs (Access Control Lists) for Active Directory objects. Below is a list of the PowerShell commands they ran.</p>
		<div id="crayon-6719ab9d223a8668136019" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-mac print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

Furthermore, they tried distributing and running malware through the task scheduler and modified group policies to save malicious tasks for the entire domain.</p>
<h3 id="defense-evasion">Defense Evasion</h3>
<p>To avoid detection, the attackers disguised their malware and tasks under the names of existing products or services.</p>
		<div id="crayon-6719ab9d223ab744345171" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-mac print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>

C:\Windows\System32\Tasks\Update Microsoft

<h2 id="unified-kill-chain-through">Unified Kill Chain: Through</h2>
<p>The Through stage in terms of the Unified Cyber​ Kill Chain refers to adversary actions within a previously compromised target network aimed at gaining access to further systems and data that the attacker needs to achieve their goals. This stage involves a series of steps designed to propagate across the network and access critical assets.</p>
<h3 id="pivoting">Pivoting</h3>
<p>The adversary used ngrok to tunnel traffic. They installed that utility immediately after connecting to the system, and set port 3389 (standard RDP port) in the configuration file. After that, all illegitimate connections to the system via RDP were made through ngrok. The attackers attached the utility to a service named &#8220;svchost&#8221; with the following command:</p>
		<div id="crayon-6719ab9d223b2626725038" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-mac print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
C:\ProgramData\svchost\svchost.exe service run --config 
C:\ProgramData\svchost\svchost.yml</textarea></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-6719ab9d223b2626725038-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-6719ab9d223b2626725038-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6719ab9d223b2626725038-1"><span class="crayon-i">C</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">ProgramData</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">svchost</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">svchost</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-e">exe </span><span class="crayon-e">service </span><span class="crayon-i">run</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>--<span class="crayon-i">config</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-6719ab9d223b2626725038-2"><span class="crayon-i">C</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">ProgramData</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">svchost</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">svchost</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">yml</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>

			<span id="crayon-6719ab9d223b3254965823" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">C</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">ProgramData</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">svchost</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span></span></span> was a directory created by the attackers. The svchost.exe file is ngrok itself, while svchost.yml serves as its configuration file. In addition to the port number, it contains an authorization token, which looks as follows: 2YXVHSiK9hhc4aKCbH4i6BLh21J_6zwxt**********. Tokens differ between samples.</p>
<p><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184142/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_09.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-113917" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184142/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_09-1024x449.png" alt="" width="1024" height="449" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184142/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_09-1024x449.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184142/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_09-300x132.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184142/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_09-768x337.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184142/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_09-1536x673.png 1536w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184142/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_09-798x350.png 798w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184142/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_09-740x324.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184142/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_09-639x280.png 639w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184142/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_09-800x351.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184142/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_09.png 1811w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a></p>
<p>The ::::%16777216 value in the Source Network Address field, in the RDP event log indicates that the attackers initiated their connections via ngrok.</p>
<h3 id="discovery">Discovery</h3>
<p>The adversary used Advanced IP Scanner, BloodHound and adPEAS to reconnoiter the LAN and domain infrastructure, and to investigate the relationships between domains. Advanced IP Scanner can quickly identify all devices on a given network. BloodHound is used to analyze and visualize users and systems the domain trusts, and to identify paths of least resistance for privilege escalation. adPEAS is used to attack Active Directory, detect configuration flaws and identify ways to escalate domain privileges. Combined, these tools allow attackers to effectively probe and exploit victims&#8217; LANs.</p>
<p>In addition, the group used PowerView module cmdlets to discover domain user accounts.</p>
		<div id="crayon-6719ab9d223b4092417037" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-mac print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

The group used PowerShell to gain domain groups data.</p>

<h3 id="privilege-escalation">Privilege Escalation</h3>
<p>To escalate privileges, the adversary primarily used the legitimate credentials of users with administrative access privileges.</p>
<p>In addition, they used the PowerView module to modify the attributes of new accounts they set up to achieve their goals:</p>
		<div id="crayon-6719ab9d223b7000359883" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-mac print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
Add-DomainObjectAcl -Rights 'All'</textarea></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-6719ab9d223b7000359883-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6719ab9d223b7000359883-1"><span class="crayon-i">Add</span>-<span class="crayon-i">DomainObjectAcl</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>-<span class="crayon-i">Rights</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">'All'</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
The -Rights &#8216;All&#8217; parameter grants the account full access to the specified object. This may include permission to read, write, create, delete and perform various operations on the object.</p>
<div id="attachment_113918" style="width: 1034px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184325/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_20.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113918" class="size-large wp-image-113918" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184325/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_20-1024x660.png" alt="Example of permissions granted with PowerView to an account of interest to the attackers" width="1024" height="660" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184325/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_20-1024x660.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184325/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_20-300x193.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184325/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_20-768x495.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184325/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_20-543x350.png 543w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184325/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_20-740x477.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184325/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_20-434x280.png 434w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184325/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_20-800x516.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184325/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_20.png 1083w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113918" class="wp-caption-text">Example of permissions granted with PowerView to an account of interest to the attackers</p></div>
<h3 id="execution">Execution</h3>
<h4 id="scripts-and-commands">Scripts and commands</h4>
<p>The adversary used system interpreters and publicly available tools, as well as self-written .bat and PowerShell scripts, to perform various actions in the system.</p>
<p>Below are some examples of attack scripts we discovered:</p>

<h4 id="sophos_kill_local-ps1">Sophos_kill_local.ps1</h4>
<p>A script we detected attempts to terminate Sophos processes on the computer and writes the results to local and remote log files.</p>
		<div id="crayon-6719ab9d223bb191621730" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-mac print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
$LogTime = Get-Date -Format "MM-dd-yyyy_hh-mm-ss"
$path = "C:\Program Files (x86)\Sophos\Logs\"
$pcname = $env:computername
$Processes = Get-WmiObject -Class Win32_Process -ComputerName $env:computername -Filter "ExecutablePath LIKE '%Sophos%'"
foreach ($process in $processes) {
  $ProcessName = $process.name
  $returnval = $process.terminate()
  $processid = $process.handle
  if($returnval.returnvalue -eq 0) {
	$LogFile1 = 'C:\Program Files (x86)\Sophos\Logs\'+$LogTime+"_Success-Terminated"+".txt"
	$LogFile11 = '\\[redacted]\NETLOGON\Sophos\Logs\'+$pcname+"_"+$LogTime+"_Success-Terminated"+".txt"
	"The process $ProcessName ($processid) has been terminated successfully." | Out-File $LogFile1 -Append -Force
	"The process $ProcessName ($processid) has been terminated successfully." | Out-File $LogFile11 -Append -Force
  } else {
	$LogFile2 = 'C:\Program Files (x86)\Sophos\Logs\'+$LogTime+"_Sophos Not-Terminated"+".txt"
	$LogFile22 = '\\[redacted]\NETLOGON\Sophos\Logs\'+$pcname+"_"+$LogTime+"_Sophos Not-Terminated"+".txt"
	"The process $ProcessName ($processid) has not been terminated." | Out-File $LogFile2 -Append -Force
	"The process $ProcessName ($processid) has not been terminated." | Out-File $LogFile22 -Append -Force
  }
 }</textarea></div>

<h4 id="using-the-task-scheduler">Using the Task Scheduler</h4>
<p>To perform all the ultimate destructive actions, such as starting the ransomware and wipers, the adversary used Scheduler tasks set up by modifying group policies. This enabled the adversary to execute these on all machines in the domain at the same time.</p>

<h3 id="credential-access">Credential Access</h3>
<p>The adversary used mimikatz to obtain user credentials. They saved the utility file under the name calculator.exe to disguise its real purpose. However, they did not bother to change the utility&#8217;s default icon. The attackers used mimikatz to set up a dump of local credentials from the memory of the lsass.exe process.</p>
<div id="attachment_113919" style="width: 1034px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184834/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_11.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113919" class="size-large wp-image-113919" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184834/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_11-1024x588.png" alt="Screenshot of calculator.exe running" width="1024" height="588" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184834/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_11-1024x588.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184834/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_11-300x172.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184834/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_11-768x441.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184834/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_11-610x350.png 610w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184834/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_11-740x425.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184834/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_11-488x280.png 488w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184834/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_11-800x459.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19184834/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_11.png 1052w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113919" class="wp-caption-text">Screenshot of calculator.exe running</p></div>

			</div>
		</div><p>
To extract additional credentials from the system, the attackers then used the console version of XenArmor&#8217;s All-In-One Password Recovery Pro utility, which can extract most of a user&#8217;s credentials from registry hives.</p>
<p>The command to collect data with All-In-One Password Recovery Pro is shown below:</p>
		<div id="crayon-6719ab9d223c0125473286" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-mac print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
c:\programdata\update\xenallpasswordpro.exe"  -a 
"c:\programdata\update\report.html"</textarea></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6719ab9d223c0125473286-1"><span class="crayon-i">c</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">programdata</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">update</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">xenallpasswordpro</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">exe</span><span class="crayon-s">"&nbsp;&nbsp;-a </span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-6719ab9d223c0125473286-2"><span class="crayon-s">"</span><span class="crayon-i">c</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">programdata</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">update</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">report</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">html</span>"</div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
In the screenshot below, you can see an example of running this utility with the parameters that the attackers used, and a list of data that it collects when configured like that.</p>
<p><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185139/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_19.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-113920" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185139/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_19.png" alt="" width="765" height="1016" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185139/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_19.png 765w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185139/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_19-226x300.png 226w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185139/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_19-264x350.png 264w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185139/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_19-740x983.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185139/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_19-211x280.png 211w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185139/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_19-678x900.png 678w" sizes="(max-width: 765px) 100vw, 765px" /></a></p>
<h3 id="lateral-movement">Lateral Movement</h3>
<p>To move within the victim&#8217;s infrastructure, the adversary used local and domain credentials obtained in earlier phases of the attack.</p>
<p>In most cases, they connected to new devices on the victim&#8217;s network via the Remote Desktop Protocol (RDP) by using the mstsc.exe executable file. They would occasionally use PsExec to move across the network via SMB and use the Enter-PSSession command to start an interactive session with remote computers on the network, a PowerShell feature for managing and running commands on remote systems with the help of PowerShell Remoting.</p>
		<div id="crayon-6719ab9d223c2399128439" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-mac print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
Enter-PSSession -ComputerName [COMPUTER 1]
Enter-PSSession -ComputerName [COMPUTER 2]
Enter-PSSession -ComputerName [COMPUTER 3]</textarea></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-6719ab9d223c2399128439-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-6719ab9d223c2399128439-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-6719ab9d223c2399128439-3">3</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6719ab9d223c2399128439-1"><span class="crayon-i">Enter</span>-<span class="crayon-i">PSSession</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>-<span class="crayon-i">ComputerName</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-i">COMPUTER</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">1</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-6719ab9d223c2399128439-2"><span class="crayon-i">Enter</span>-<span class="crayon-i">PSSession</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>-<span class="crayon-i">ComputerName</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-i">COMPUTER</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">2</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6719ab9d223c2399128439-3"><span class="crayon-i">Enter</span>-<span class="crayon-i">PSSession</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>-<span class="crayon-i">ComputerName</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-i">COMPUTER</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">3</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
Enter-PSSession sets up a temporary interactive session between the local and remote systems, allowing the adversary to run PowerShell commands directly on remote machines as if running them locally. The communication process typically uses the WS-Management protocol running on top of HTTP or HTTPS.</p>
<h2 id="unified-kill-chain-out">Unified Kill Chain: Out</h2>
<p>The Exit stage in terms of the Unified Kill Chain describes the adversary&#8217;s concluding actions after successfully infiltrating the target network and gaining access to all systems and data they are looking to access. This stage focuses on achieving the ultimate goals of the attack, which may include data theft, sabotage or other actions that compromise the confidentiality, integrity and availability (CIA) of the victim&#8217;s information assets.</p>
<h3 id="collection">Collection</h3>
<p>The adversary collected substantial amounts of sensitive information about their victims: financial documents, technical drawings, corporate email, and so on. They used 7z to archive data they collected and forwarded the data via cloud sharing services.</p>
<p>Also during their attacks, the adversary archived and exfiltrated the Telegram data folder (tdata).</p>
		<div id="crayon-6719ab9d223c3514000665" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-mac print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
C:\Users\[User]\AppData\Roaming\Telegram Desktop\tdata\tdata.7z</textarea></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-6719ab9d223c3514000665-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6719ab9d223c3514000665-1"><span class="crayon-i">C</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">Users</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-i">User</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">AppData</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">Roaming</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-e">Telegram </span><span class="crayon-i">Desktop</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">tdata</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">tdata</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-cn">7z</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
This folder contains cached media files (images, videos, audio), messages, stickers and documents the user has sent or received via Telegram. The data can be used for quick access without having to download files again from the servers. The tdata folder also contains session files that allow the application to automatically connect to the account without the user having to reenter their login and password.</p>
<p>An adversary who gains access to the folder can extract private messages, media files and documents, which results in the leakage of sensitive personal or commercial information. The adversary can leverage session files and encryption keys to bypass authentication when signing in to a Telegram account, to read chats and to impersonate the victim when sending messages.</p>
<h3 id="exfiltration">Exfiltration</h3>
<p>The adversary uploaded archives containing data they were interested in to <a href="https://dropmefiles.net/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://dropmefiles.net/</a> via a browser. We learned that DropMeFiles was the file sharing service they used when we found a page header that read, &#8220;Завантаження вдалося! &#8211; <a href="http://dropmefiles.net" target="_blank" rel="noopener">dropmefiles.net</a>&#8221; (&#8220;Upload successful!&#8221; &#8211; <a href="http://dropmefiles.net" target="_blank" rel="noopener">dropmefiles.net</a>) in the browser cache in the aftermath of an attack.</p>
<p><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185320/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_15.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-113921" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185320/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_15.png" alt="" width="978" height="980" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185320/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_15.png 978w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185320/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_15-300x300.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185320/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_15-150x150.png 150w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185320/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_15-768x770.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185320/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_15-349x350.png 349w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185320/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_15-740x742.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185320/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_15-279x280.png 279w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185320/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_15-800x802.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185320/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_15-50x50.png 50w" sizes="(max-width: 978px) 100vw, 978px" /></a></p>
<h3 id="impact">Impact</h3>
<h4 id="ransomware">Ransomware</h4>
<p>The attackers used a version of the popular LockBit 3.0 ransomware, compiled from publicly available source code, to encrypt the data.</p>
<div id="attachment_113922" style="width: 1034px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185408/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_02.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113922" class="size-large wp-image-113922" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185408/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_02-1024x147.png" alt="Kaspersky Threat Attribution Engine attribution" width="1024" height="147" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185408/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_02-1024x147.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185408/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_02-300x43.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185408/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_02-768x111.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185408/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_02-1536x221.png 1536w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185408/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_02-740x107.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185408/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_02-1600x230.png 1600w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185408/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_02-800x115.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185408/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_02.png 1855w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113922" class="wp-caption-text">Kaspersky Threat Attribution Engine attribution</p></div>
<p>We detected ransomware files at the following paths:</p>
<ul>
<li>\ProgramData\;</li>
<li>\\netlogon\.</li>
</ul>
<p>The following file names featured in known incidents involving LockBit 3.0 ransomware.</p>
<ul>
<li>twelve.exe;</li>
<li>1.exe;</li>
<li>12.exe;</li>
<li>enc.exe;</li>
<li>betta.exe;</li>
<li>sed.exe;</li>
<li>svo.exe.</li>
</ul>
<p>Below is a detonation graph for the ransomware, built by <a href="https://media.kaspersky.com/en/business-security/enterprise/datasheet-kaspersky-cloud-sandbox-eng.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Kaspersky Cloud Sandbox</a>. It displays file execution and suspicious events that occur in the process. As you can see from the graph, the ransomware is quite noisy and generates a lot of events that give away its activity.</p>
<div id="attachment_113923" style="width: 1034px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185709/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_22.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113923" class="size-large wp-image-113923" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185709/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_22-1024x518.png" alt="Detonation graph for the ransomware used by Twelve" width="1024" height="518" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185709/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_22-1024x518.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185709/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_22-300x152.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185709/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_22-768x389.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185709/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_22-691x350.png 691w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185709/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_22-740x375.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185709/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_22-553x280.png 553w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185709/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_22-800x405.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185709/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_22.png 1373w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113923" class="wp-caption-text">Detonation graph for the ransomware used by Twelve</p></div>
<p>As previously mentioned under Execution, the ransomware leverages group policies to spread across its victims&#8217; infrastructures. The attackers used PowerShell to move the ransomware file to the netlogon network share and then ran a script to modify group policies.</p>
		<div id="crayon-6719ab9d223c5040527386" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-mac print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>

powershell.exe -ex bypass -f C:\Users\Public\gpo.ps1</textarea></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-6719ab9d223c5040527386-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6719ab9d223c5040527386-1"><span class="crayon-i">powershell</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">exe</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>-<span class="crayon-e">ex </span><span class="crayon-i">bypass</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>-<span class="crayon-i">f</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">C</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">Users</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-m">Public</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">gpo</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">ps1</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
After updating the policies, they set up scheduled tasks on all domain computers to copy and run the ransomware.</p>
<p><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_08.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-113924" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_08.png" alt="" width="760" height="418" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_08.png 760w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_08-300x165.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_08-270x150.png 270w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_08-636x350.png 636w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_08-740x407.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19185814/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_08-509x280.png 509w" sizes="(max-width: 760px) 100vw, 760px" /></a></p>
<p>First, the ransomware was moved from the netlogon network share to the local ProgramData directory by the Copywiper task as follows:</p>
		<div id="crayon-6719ab9d223c6356877060" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-mac print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
powershell.exe Copy-Item `\\[DOMAIN]\netlogon\twelve.exe` -Destination `C:\ProgramData`</textarea></div>

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6719ab9d223c6356877060-1"><span class="crayon-i">powershell</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-e">exe </span><span class="crayon-i">Copy</span>-<span class="crayon-i">Item</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">`</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-i">DOMAIN</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">netlogon</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">twelve</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">exe</span><span class="crayon-sy">`</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>-<span class="crayon-i">Destination</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">`</span><span class="crayon-i">C</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">ProgramData</span><span class="crayon-sy">`</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>

			</div>
		</div><p>
After this, they started the ransomware from a local folder or network share via the CLI, specifying a unique password as the -pass argument:</p>
