</table>
<p>Interestingly, the configuration for creating a ransom note lacks any contacts or ways of reaching out to the attackers. The final note consists of just the group logo.</p>
<p><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190831/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_16.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-113926" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190831/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_16.png" alt="" width="803" height="932" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190831/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_16.png 803w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190831/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_16-258x300.png 258w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190831/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_16-768x891.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190831/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_16-302x350.png 302w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190831/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_16-740x859.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190831/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_16-241x280.png 241w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190831/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_16-775x900.png 775w" sizes="(max-width: 803px) 100vw, 803px" /></a></p>
<p>We also found that in some cases, attackers used a Trojan made from a leaked builder for the Chaos ransomware to encrypt files. We discovered samples of that ransomware at the following paths:</p>
<table width="100%">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>c:\netlogon\enc.exe</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>c:\Users\User\enc.exe</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>c:\Windows\System32\config\systemprofile\appdata\roaming\twelve.exe</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>c:\Windows\sysvol\domain\scripts\enc.exe</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p>As you can see from the screenshot below, the Kaspersky Threat Attribution Engine detects that one of these samples bears 60% similarity to Chaos.</p>
<div id="attachment_113927" style="width: 974px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190928/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_04.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113927" class="size-full wp-image-113927" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190928/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_04.png" alt="Result of the Kaspersky Threat Attribution Engine file attribution" width="964" height="465" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190928/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_04.png 964w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190928/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_04-300x145.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190928/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_04-768x370.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190928/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_04-726x350.png 726w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190928/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_04-740x357.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190928/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_04-580x280.png 580w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19190928/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_04-800x386.png 800w" sizes="(max-width: 964px) 100vw, 964px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113927" class="wp-caption-text">Result of the Kaspersky Threat Attribution Engine file attribution</p></div>
<p>At the time we discovered the samples, it was unclear who was behind the incidents in which they were used. However, static analysis showed that the code contained characteristic lines linking the samples to the Twelve group.</p>
<div id="attachment_113928" style="width: 1034px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191106/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_18.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113928" class="size-large wp-image-113928" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191106/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_18-1024x511.png" alt="Result of the static analysis of Chaos-based ransomware" width="1024" height="511" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191106/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_18-1024x511.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191106/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_18-300x150.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191106/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_18-768x383.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191106/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_18-702x350.png 702w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191106/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_18-740x369.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191106/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_18-561x280.png 561w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191106/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_18-800x399.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191106/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_18.png 1181w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113928" class="wp-caption-text">Result of the static analysis of Chaos-based ransomware</p></div>
<h4 id="wipers">Wipers</h4>
<p>In addition to the ransomware, the adversary used wipers to destroy their victims&#8217; infrastructures. They typically ran the wipers after encrypting files.</p>
<p>The wiper file we found had been compiled from publicly available source code. The wiper rewrites the master boot record (MBR) on connected drives so when the victim next turns on the device, the &#8220;From Iran with love &#8211; Shamoon&#8221; message appears on the screen, and the operating system will not load.</p>
<div id="attachment_113929" style="width: 1005px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191211/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_06.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113929" class="size-full wp-image-113929" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191211/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_06.png" alt="String written to the MBR" width="995" height="112" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191211/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_06.png 995w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191211/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_06-300x34.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191211/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_06-768x86.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191211/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_06-990x112.png 990w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191211/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_06-740x83.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191211/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_06-800x90.png 800w" sizes="(max-width: 995px) 100vw, 995px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113929" class="wp-caption-text">String written to the MBR</p></div>
<p>The file then recursively goes through each directory, except for Windows and System Volume Information, on all mounted drives, and does the following for each file:</p>
<ul>
<li>Overwrite the file contents with randomly generated bytes;</li>
<li>Overwrite file metadata: reset size and set random created/modified/opened dates;</li>
<li>Assign a random name to the file and delete it.</li>
</ul>
<p>When done, the malicious file deletes itself and shuts down the system.</p>
<p>As we conducted our dynamic and static analyses, we concluded that the wiper version was identical to the publicly available one.</p>
<div id="attachment_113930" style="width: 1034px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191302/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_14.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113930" class="size-large wp-image-113930" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191302/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_14-1024x405.png" alt="Wiper detonation graph in Kaspersky Cloud SandBox" width="1024" height="405" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191302/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_14-1024x405.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191302/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_14-300x119.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191302/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_14-768x303.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191302/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_14-886x350.png 886w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191302/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_14-740x292.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191302/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_14-709x280.png 709w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191302/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_14-800x316.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191302/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_14.png 1392w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113930" class="wp-caption-text">Wiper detonation graph in Kaspersky Cloud SandBox</p></div>
<div id="attachment_113931" style="width: 1034px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191752/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_21.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113931" class="size-large wp-image-113931" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191752/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_21-1024x383.png" alt="Result of the wiper static analysis" width="1024" height="383" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191752/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_21-1024x383.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191752/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_21-300x112.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191752/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_21-768x288.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191752/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_21-935x350.png 935w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191752/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_21-740x277.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191752/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_21-748x280.png 748w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191752/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_21-800x300.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191752/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_21.png 1533w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113931" class="wp-caption-text">Result of the wiper static analysis</p></div>
<p>Also while researching the attacks by Twelve, we discovered another version of the wiper. The sample was identical to Shamoon, except for a number of specifically renamed functions.</p>
<div id="attachment_113932" style="width: 618px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191836/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_12.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113932" class="size-full wp-image-113932" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191836/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_12.png" alt="Renamed Shamoon-based wiper features" width="608" height="317" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191836/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_12.png 608w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191836/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_12-300x156.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19191836/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_12-537x280.png 537w" sizes="(max-width: 608px) 100vw, 608px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113932" class="wp-caption-text">Renamed Shamoon-based wiper features</p></div>
<p>While investigating attacks by the group, we found wiper files at the following paths:</p>
<ul>
<li>\Desktop\;</li>
<li>\ProgramData\;</li>
<li>\\netlogon\.</li>
</ul>
<p>The following file names have featured in known incidents involving the wiper:</p>
<ul>
<li>intel.exe;</li>
<li>mail.exe;</li>
<li>wiper.exe.</li>
</ul>
<p>The wiper&#8217;s spread pattern across a victim&#8217;s infrastructure is almost no different from that of the ransomware. The adversary uses PowerShell to copy the wiper file to the netlogon network share and then runs a script that modifies group policies and creates scheduled tasks.</p>

			</div>
		</div><p>
The wiper file is then copied from the netlogon network share to the local ProgramData folder on all previously encrypted domain computers.</p>
		<div id="crayon-6719ab9d223d0612135264" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-mac print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
After this, a scheduled task starts and runs the wiper file, which destroys data on the device.</p>
		<div id="crayon-6719ab9d223d1908555634" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-mac print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
C:\ProgramData\intel.exe</textarea></div>

					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-6719ab9d223d1908555634-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6719ab9d223d1908555634-1"><span class="crayon-i">C</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">ProgramData</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">intel</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">exe</span></div></div></td>

		</div><p>
<div id="attachment_113933" style="width: 1034px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19192228/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_07.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113933" class="size-large wp-image-113933" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19192228/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_07-1024x427.png" alt="Wiper spread pattern in the victim's infrastructure" width="1024" height="427" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19192228/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_07-1024x427.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19192228/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_07-300x125.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19192228/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_07-768x320.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19192228/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_07-1536x641.png 1536w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19192228/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_07-839x350.png 839w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19192228/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_07-740x309.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19192228/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_07-671x280.png 671w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19192228/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_07-800x334.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19192228/twelve_group_unified_kill_chain_07.png 1848w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113933" class="wp-caption-text">Wiper spread pattern in the victim&#8217;s infrastructure</p></div>
<h3 id="objectives">Objectives</h3>
<p>The threat actor&#8217;s strategic goals:</p>
<ul>
<li>Destroy critical assets and disrupt business;</li>
<li>Steal sensitive data;</li>
<li>Discredit victims by reporting the compromise on the attackers&#8217; Telegram channel.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="takeaways">Takeaways</h2>
<p>Twelve is mainly driven by hacktivism rather than financial gain. This shows in their modus operandi: rather than demand a ransom for decrypting data, Twelve prefers to encrypt victims&#8217; data and then destroy their infrastructure with a wiper to prevent recovery. The approach is indicative of a desire to cause maximum damage to target organizations without deriving direct financial benefit.</p>
<p>Our analysis also shows that the group sticks to a publicly available and familiar arsenal of malware tools, which suggests it makes none of its own. This makes it possible to detect and prevent Twelve&#8217;s attacks in due time. Failure to do so could result in the organization&#8217;s infrastructure sustaining significant damage from the threat actor.</p>
